\\t\\t\\t})\\n350: \\t\\t} else {\\n351: \\t\\t\\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\\n352: \\t\\t}\\n353: \\t}\\n354: klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n688: \\t// Extenders are called sequentially.\\n689: \\t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\\n690: \\t// extender in a // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\\n746: \\tctx context.Context,\\n747: \\textenders []framework.Extender,\\n748: \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n611: \t\tstatus := fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)\n612: \t\tif status.Code() == framework.Error {\n613: \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons []string\n715: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; found {\n716: \t\t\t\taggregatedReasons = statuses[failedNodeName].Reasons()\n717: \t\t\t}\n718: \t\t\taggregatedReasons = append(aggregatedReasons, failedMsg)\n719: \t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, aggregatedReasons...)\n720: \t\t}\n721: \n722: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedMap {\n723: \t\t\tif _, found := failedAndUnresolvableMap[failedNodeName]; found {\n724: \t\t\t\t// failedAndUnresolvableMap takes precedence over failedMap\n725: \t\t\t\t// note that this only happens if the extender returns the node in both maps\n726: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n727: \t\t\t}\n728: \t\t\tif _, found := statuses[failedNodeName]; !found {\n729: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName] = framework.NewStatus(framework.Unschedulable, failedMsg)\n730: \t\t\t} else {\n731: \t\t\t\tstatuses[failedNodeName].AppendReason(failedMsg)\n732: \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the required format\n756: \tif len(extenders) == 0 && !fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n757: \t\tresult := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, len(nodes))\n758: \t\tfor i := range nodes {\n759: \t\t\tresult = append(result, framework.NodePluginScores{\n760: \t\t\t\tName:       nodes[i].Node().Name,\n761: \t\t\t\tTotalScore: 1,\n762: \t\t\t})\n763: \t\t}\n764: \t\treturn result, nil\n765: \t}\n766: \n767: \t// Run PreScore plugins.\n768: \tpreScoreStatus := fwk.RunPreScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n769: \tif !preScoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n770: \t\treturn nil, preScoreStatus.AsError()\n771: \t}\n772: \n773: \t// Run the Score plugins.\n774: \tnodesScores, scoreStatus := fwk.RunScorePlugins(ctx, state, pod, nodes)\n775: \tif !scoreStatus.IsSuccess() {\n776: \t\treturn nil, scoreStatus.AsError()\n777: \t}\n778: \n779: \t// Additional details logged at level 10 if enabled.\n780: \tloggerVTen := logger.V(10)\n781: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n782: \t\tfor _, nodeScore := range nodesScores {\n783: \t\t\tfor _, pluginScore := range nodeScore.Scores {\n784: \t\t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Plugin scored node for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"plugin\", pluginScore.Name, \"node\", nodeScore.Name, \"score\", pluginScore.Score)\n785: \t\t\t}\n786: \t\t}\n787: \t}\n788: \n789: \tif len(extenders) != 0 && nodes != nil {\n790: \t\t// allNodeExtendersScores has all extenders scores for all nodes.\n791: \t\t// It is keyed with node name.\n792: \t\tallNodeExtendersScores := make(map[string]*framework.NodePluginScores, len(nodes))\n793: \t\tvar mu sync.Mutex\n794: \t\tvar wg sync.WaitGroup\n795: \t\tfor i := range extenders {\n796: \t\t\tif !extenders[i].IsInterested(pod) {\n797: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n798: \t\t\t}\n799: \t\t\twg.Add(1)\n800: \t\t\tgo func(extIndex int) {\n801: \t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Inc()\n802: \t\t\t\tdefer func() {\n803: \t\t\t\t\tmetrics.Goroutines.WithLabelValues(metrics.PrioritizingExtender).Dec()\n804: \t\t\t\t\twg.Done()\n805: \t\t\t\t}()\n806: \t\t\t\tprioritizedList, weight, err := \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n39: \\t\\\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/apis/config\\\"\\n40: \\t\\\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/framework/parallelize\\\"\\n41: )\\n42: \\n43: // NodeScoreList declares a list of nodes and their scores.\\n44: type NodeScoreList []NodeScore\\n45: \\n46: // NodeScore is a struct with node name and score.\\n47: type NodeScore struct {\\n48: \\tName  string\\n49: \\tScore int64\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // NodeToStatusMap declares map from node name to its status.\\n53: type NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status\\n54: \\n55: // NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\\n56: type NodePluginScores struct {\\n57: \\t// Name is node name.\\n58: \\tName string\\n59: \\t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\\n60: \\tScores []PluginScore\\n61: \\t// TotalScore is the total score in Scores.\\n62: \\tTotalScore int64\\n63: }\\n64: \\n65: // PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\\n66: type PluginScore struct {\\n67: \\t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\\n68: \\tName  string\\n69: \\tScore int64\\n70: }\\n71: \\n72: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\\n73: type Code int\\n74: \\n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n77: const (\\n78: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n79: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n80: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n81: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n82: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n83: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n84: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n85: \\tError\\n86: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n87: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n88: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n89: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n90: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n94: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n95: \\tUnschedulable\\n96: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n97: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n98: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n99: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n100: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n101: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n104: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n105: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n106: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n107: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n108: \\tWait\\n109: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n110: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n111: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n112: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n118: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n119: \\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\\n120: \\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\\n121: \\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n122: \\t//\\n123: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n124: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\\n125: \\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\\n126: \\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\\n127: \\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\\n128: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\\n129: \\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\\n130: \\tPending\\n131: )\\n132: \\n133: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\\n134: var codes = []string{\\\"Success\\\", \\\"Error\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\", \\\"Wait\\\", \\\"Skip\\\", \\\"Pending\\\"}\\n135: \\n136: func (c plugins.\\n73: type Code int\\n74: \\n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n77: const (\\n78: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n79: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n80: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n81: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n82: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n83: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n84: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n85: \\tError\\n86: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n87: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n88: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n89: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n90: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n94: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n95: \\tUnschedulable\\n96: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n97: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n98: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n99: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n100: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n101: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n104: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n105: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n106: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n107: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n108: \\tWait\\n109: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n110: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n111: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n112: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n118: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n119: \\t// It's different from when to component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n122: \\t//\\n123: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n124: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\n73: type Code int\n74: \n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\n77: const (\n78: \t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n79: \t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n80: \tSuccess Code = iota\n81: \t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n82: \t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n83: \t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n84: \t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n85: \tError\n86: \t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n87: \t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n88: \t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n89: \t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n90: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n91: \t//\n92: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n93: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n94: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n95: \tUnschedulable\n96: \t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n97: \t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n98: \t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n99: \t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n100: \t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n101: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n102: \t//\n103: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n104: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n105: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n106: \tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n107: \t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n108: \tWait\n109: \t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n110: \t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n111: \t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n112: \t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n113: \tSkip\n114: \t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n115: \t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n116: \t//\n117: \t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n118: \t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n119: \t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n120: \t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n121: \t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n122: \t//\n123: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n124: \t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n125: \t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n126: \t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n127: \t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n128: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n129: \t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n130: \tPending\n131: )\n132: \n133: If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n430: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n431: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n432: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n433: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n434: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n435: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n436: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n437: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n438: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n439: }\\n440: \\n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. These plugins are called\n442: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n443: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n444: \tPlugin\n445: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n446: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n447: \t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\n448: \t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\n449: \t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n450: \t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n451: \t//\n452: \t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\n453: \t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n454: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n455: \t//\n456: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n457: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n458: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n459: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n460: \t//\n461: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n462: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n463: \t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n464: \t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n465: \tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n466: }\n467: \n468: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n469: // informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n470: // that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n471: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\n472: type PreScorePlugin interface {\n473: \tPlugin\n474: \t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n475: \t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n476: \t// the pod will be rejected\n477: \t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n478: \t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n479: \tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n480: }\n481: \n482: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\n483: type ScoreExtensions interface {\n484: \t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n485: \t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n486: \t// a success status.\n487: \tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n488: }\n489: \n490: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n491: // nodes that passed the filtering phase.\n492: type ScorePlugin interface {\n493: \tPlugin\n494: \t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\n495: \t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\n496: \t// the pod will be rejected.\n497: \tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\n498: \n499: \t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n500: \tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\n501: }\n502: \n503: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n504: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n505: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n506: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n507: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n508: // rejection of the pod.\n509: type ReservePlugin interface {\n510: \tPlugin\n511: \t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n512: \t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\n513: \t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\n514: \tReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n515: \t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\n516: \t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\n517: \t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\n518: \t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\n519: \t// method for the same plugin was not called.\n520: \tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n521: }\n522: \n523: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreBind\" plugins.\n524: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\n525: type PreBindPlugin interface {\n526: \tPlugin\n527: \t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\n528: \t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\n529: \tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n530: }\n531: \n532: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PostBind\" plugins.\n533: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\n534: type PostBindPlugin interface {\n535: \tPlugin\n536: \t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\n537: \t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\n538: \t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\n539: \t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\n540: \tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n541: }\n542: \n543: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Permit\" plugins.\n544: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\n545: type PermitPlugin interface {\n546: \tPlugin\n547: \t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\n548: \t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n549: \t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n550: \t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n551: \t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \"wait\", the framework will wait only\n552: \t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\n553: \tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\n554: }\n555: \n556: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Bind\" plugins. Bind\n557: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\n558: type BindPlugin interface {\n559: \tPlugin\n560: \t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n561: \t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n562: \t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\n563: \t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\n564: \t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\n565: \t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\n566: \tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n567: }\n568: \n569: // Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\n570: // Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\n571: type Framework interface {\n572: \tHandle\n573: \n574: \t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\n575: \tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\n576: \n577: \t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\n578: \tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\n579: \n580: \t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\n581: \tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\n582: \n583: \t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. It returns\n584: \t// *Status and its code is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\n585: \t// anything but Success. If a non-success status is returned, then the scheduling\n586: \t// cycle is aborted.\n587: \t// It also returns a PreFilterResult, which may influence what or how many nodes to\n588: \t// evaluate downstream.\n589: \tRunPreFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n590: \n591: \t// RunPostFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PostFilter plugins.\n592: \t// PostFilter plugins can either be informational, in which case should be configured\n593: \t// to execute first and return Unschedulable status, or ones that try to change the\n594: \t// cluster state to make the pod potentially schedulable in a future scheduling cycle.\n595: \tRunPostFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n596: \n597: \t// RunPreBindPlugins runs the set of configured PreBind plugins. It returns\n598: \t// *Status and its code is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\n599: \t// anything but Success. In either case the pod is not going to be bound.\n602: \tRunPreBindPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n603: \n604: \t// RunPostBindPlugins runs the set of configured PostBind plugins.\n605: \tRunPostBindPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n606: \n607: \t// RunReservePluginsReserve runs the Reserve method of the set of\n608: \t// configured Reserve plugins. In\n610: \t// such case, pod will not be scheduled.\n611: \tRunReservePluginsReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n612: \n613: \t// RunReservePluginsUnreserve runs the Unreserve method of the set of\n614: \t// configured Reserve plugins.\n615: \tRunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n616: \n617: \t// RunPermitPlugins runs the set of configured Permit plugins. If any of these\n618: \t// plugins returns a status other than \"Success\" or \"Wait\", it does not continue\n619: \t// running the remaining plugins and returns an error. Otherwise, if any of the\n620: \t// plugins returns \"Wait\", then this function will create and add waiting pod\n621: \t// to a map of currently waiting pods and return status with \"Wait\" code.\n622: \t// Pod will remain waiting pod for the minimum duration returned by the Permit plugins.\n623: \tRunPermitPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n624: \n625: \t// WaitOnPermit will block, if the pod is a waiting pod, until the waiting pod is rejected or allowed.\n626: \tWaitOnPermit(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod) *Status\n627: \n628: \t// RunBindPlugins runs the set of configured Bind plugins. A Bind plugin may choose\n629: \t// whether or not to handle the given Pod. If a Bind plugin chooses to skip the\n630: \t// binding, it should return code=5(\"skip\") status. Plugins\n662: // must store and use this handle to call framework functions.\n663: type Handle interface {\n664: \t// PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\n665: \tPodNominator\n666: \t// PluginsRunner abstracts operations to run some plugins.\n667: \tPluginsRunner\n668: \t// SnapshotSharedLister returns listers from the latest NodeInfo Snapshot. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01MmYTBSpMBaRrTJUkMFbc8C","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\\n3: \\n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \\\"License\\\");\\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n7: \\n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n9: \\n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: package cache\\n18: \\n19: import (\\n20: \\tv1 \\\"k8s.io/api/core/v1\\\"\\n21: \\t\\\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/sets\\\"\\n22: \\t\\\"k8s.io/klog/v2\\\"\\n23: \\t\\\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/framework\\\"\\n24: )\\n25: \\n26: // Cache collects pods' information and provides node-level aggregated information.\\n27: // It's intended for generic scheduler to do efficient lookup.\\n28: // Cache's operations are pod centric. It does incremental updates based on pod events.\\n29: // Pod events are sent via network. We don't have guaranteed delivery of all events:\\n30: // We use Reflector to list and watch from remote.\\n31: // Reflector might be slow and do a relist, which would lead to missing events.\\n32: //\\n33: // State Machine of a pod's events in scheduler's cache:\\n34: //\\n35: //\\t+-------------------------------------------+  +----+\\n36: //\\t|                            Add            |  |    |\\n37: //\\t|                                           |  |    | Update\\n38: //\\t+      Assume                Add            v  v    |\\n39: //\\n40: // Initial +--------> Assumed +------------+---> Added <--+\\n41: //\\n42: //\\t^                +   +               |       +\\n43: //\\t|                |   |               |       |\\n44: //\\t|                |   |           Add |       | Remove\\n45: //\\t|                |   |               |       |\\n46: //\\t|                |   |               +       |\\n47: //\\t+----------------+   +-----------> Expired   +----> Deleted\\n48: //\\t      Forget             Expire\\n49: //\\n50: // Note that an assumed pod can expire, because if we haven't received Add event notifying us\\n51: // for a while, there might be some problems and we shouldn't keep the pod in cache anymore.\\n52: //\\n53: // Note that \\\"Initial\\\", \\\"Expired\\\", and \\\"Deleted\\\" pods do not actually exist in cache.\\n54: // Based on existing use cases, we are making the following assumptions:\\n55: //   - No pod would be assumed twice\\n56: //   - A pod could be added without going through scheduler. In this case, we will see Add but not Assume event.\\n57: //   - If a pod wasn't added, it wouldn't be removed or updated.\\n58: //   - Both \\\"Expired\\\" and \\\"Deleted\\\" are valid end states. In case of some problems, e.g. network issue,\\n59: //     a pod might have changed its state (e.g. added and deleted) without delivering notification to the cache.\\n60: type Cache interface {\\n61: \\t// NodeCount returns the number of nodes in the cache.\\n62: \\t// DO NOT use outside of tests.\\n63: \\tNodeCount() int\\n64: \\n65: \\t// PodCount returns the number of pods in the cache (including those from deleted nodes).\\n66: \\t// DO NOT use outside of tests.\\n67: \\tPodCount() (int, error)\\n68: \\n69: \\t// AssumePod assumes a pod scheduled and aggregates the pod's information into its node.\\n70: \\t// The implementation also decides the policy to expire pod before being confirmed (receiving Add event).\\n71: \\t// After expiration, its information would be subtracted.\\n72: \\tAssumePod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n73: \\n74: \\t// FinishBinding signals that cache for assumed pod can be expired\\n75: \\tFinishBinding(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n76: \\n77: \\t// ForgetPod removes an assumed pod from cache.\\n78: \\tForgetPod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n79: \\n80: \\t// AddPod either confirms a pod if it's assumed, or adds it back if it's expired.\\n81: \\t// If added back, the pod's information would be added again.\\n82: \\tAddPod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n83: \\n84: \\t// UpdatePod removes oldPod's information and adds newPod's information.\\n85: \\tUpdatePod(logger klog.Logger, oldPod, newPod *v1.Pod) error\\n86: \\n87: \\t// RemovePod removes a pod. The pod's information would be subtracted from assigned node.\\n88: \\tRemovePod(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod) error\\n89: \\n90: \\t// GetPod returns the pod from the cache with the same namespace and the\\n91: \\t// same name of the specified pod.\\n92: \\tGetPod(pod *v1.Pod) (*v1.Pod, error)\\n93: \\n94: \\t// IsAssumedPod returns true if the pod is assumed and not expired.\\n95: \\tIsAssumedPod(pod *v1.Pod) (bool, error)\\n96: \\n97: \\t// AddNode adds overall information about node.\\n98: \\t// It returns a clone of added NodeInfo object.\\n99: \\tAddNode(logger klog.Logger, node *v1.Node) *framework.NodeInfo\\n100: \\n101: \\t// UpdateNode updates overall information about node.\\n102: \\t// It returns a clone of updated NodeInfo object.\\n103: \\tUpdateNode(logger klog.Logger, oldNode, newNode *v1.Node) *framework.NodeInfo\\n104: \\n105: \\t// RemoveNode removes overall information about node.\\n106: \\tRemoveNode(logger klog.Logger, node *v1.Node) error\\n107: \\n108: \\t// UpdateSnapshot updates the passed infoSnapshot to the current contents of Cache.\\n109: \\t// The node info contains aggregated information of pods scheduled (including assumed to be)\\n110: \\t// on this node.\\n111: \\t// The snapshot only includes Nodes that are not deleted at the time this function is called.\\n112: \\t// nodeinfo.Node() is guaranteed to be not nil for all Let me understand the flow one more time:\n\n1. **Entry Point**: ScheduleOne() in schedule_one.go - Called repeatedly in a loop by Run() in scheduler.go\n\n2. **Main Flow**:\n   - ScheduleOne gets a pod from the queue\n   - Calls schedulingCycle() - the SCHEDULING PHASE\n     - schedulingCycle calls sched.SchedulePod (which is sched.schedulePod)\n     - schedulePod does:\n       - Snapshots the cache\n       - Calls findNodesThatFitPod (filtering phase)\n         - Runs PreFilter plugins\n         - Runs Filter plugins in parallel\n       - If multiple nodes, calls prioritizeNodes (scoring phase)\n         - Runs PreScore plugins\n         - Runs Score plugins\n         - Returns scored nodes\n     - Calls assume() to add the pod to cache optimistically\n     - Runs Reserve plugins\n     - Runs Permit plugins\n   - If successful, launches bindingCycle() as a goroutine - the BINDING PHASE\n     - bindingCycle calls:\n       - WaitOnPermit (waits for Permit plugins to allow)\n       - Runs PreBind plugins\n       - Calls bind() (runs Bind plugins/extenders)\n       - Runs PostBind plugins\n\n3. **Plugin Framework** (in framework/runtime/framework.go):\n   - frameworkImpl manages all plugins\n   - Plugins are stored in arrays like preFilterPlugins, filterPlugins, scorePlugins, etc.\n   - Framework has Run* methods like RunPreFilterPlugins(), RunFilterPlugins(), etc.\n\n4. **Scheduling Queue** (in internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go):\n   - PriorityQueue with three sub-queues:\n     - activeQ - pods being actively considered\n     - backoffQ - pods that failed and are waiting in backoff\n     - unschedulablePods - pods that couldn't be scheduled\n\n5. **Cache** (in internal/cache/interface.go):\n   - Maintains node and pod state\n   - Tracks assumed pods (pods that Contains the Scheduler struct with Cache, SchedulingQueue, Profiles, and SchedulePod function. The Run() method starts the main scheduling loop.\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Main scheduling pipeline orchestration. Contains ScheduleOne() which calls schedulingCycle() and bindingCycle(). Implements schedulePod(), findNodesThatFitPod(), and the two-phase scheduling design.\n\n### Plugin Framework\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Plugin interfaces for all extension points: PreEnqueuePlugin, PreFilterPlugin, FilterPlugin, PostFilterPlugin, PreScorePlugin, ScorePlugin, ReservePlugin, PreBindPlugin, BindPlugin, PostBindPlugin, PermitPlugin. Defines Framework interface and Status codes.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — CycleState struct for storing plugin state during a scheduling cycle using sync.Map for thread-safe \"write once, read many\" access.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — frameworkImpl implementation managing plugin registration, initialization, and execution. Contains Run* methods for each extension point. Implements plugin discovery, validation, and orchestration.\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** — Plugin registry for factory functions, allows both in-tree and out-of-tree plugin registration.\n\n### Scheduling Queue & Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue interface and PriorityQueue implementation with three sub-queues: activeQ (pods being scheduled), backoffQ (backoff waiting), unschedulablePods (unschedulable pods). Implements pod nomination and in-flight tracking.\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/interface.go** — Cache interface for pod and node state management. Implements state machine: Initial → Assumed → Added/Expired → Deleted. Tracks assumed pods for optimistic scheduling.\n\n### Built-in Plugins & Utilities\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/** — In-tree plugin implementations (NodeResourcesFit, NodeAffinity, PodAffinity, Taint, etc.)\n- **pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go** — Scheduler profile management for multi-scheduler support\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/parallelize/parallelize.go** — Parallel execution utilities for filter and score operations\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Entry Point: Main Scheduling Loop\n**scheduler.go:435 Run()** → Starts SchedulingQueue and launches main scheduling loop\n- Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.Run()` to start queue processing\n- Calls `wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)` - runs ScheduleOne repeatedly until context done\n\n### 2. Pod Retrieval & Framework Selection\n**schedule_one.go:66 ScheduleOne()** → Processes one pod per invocation\n- Calls `sched.NextPod()` (which is `podQueue.Pop()`) to get next pod from queue (line 68)\n- Calls `sched.frameworkForPod(pod)` to select the appropriate framework/profile (line 86)\n- Checks `sched.skipPodSchedule()` - skips if pod is deleted or already assumed (line 93)\n- Creates `framework.CycleState` for storing plugin state (line 101)\n\n### 3. Scheduling Cycle (Phase 1: Find & Reserve)\n**schedule_one.go:139 schedulingCycle()** → Main scheduling algorithm\n- Calls `sched.SchedulePod()` which is `sched.schedulePod()` (line 149)\n  - **schedule_one.go:390 schedulePod()** → Filters and scores nodes\n    - Calls `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()` to get current node state snapshot (line 393)\n    - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod()` - performs filtering (line 402)\n      - **schedule_one.go:442 findNodesThatFitPod()** → Filters nodes via PreFilter, Filter, and extenders\n        - Calls `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()` - extension point: PreFilter (line 453)\n        - Evaluates nominated node if present (line 475)\n        - Calls `sched.findNodesThatPassFilters()` - parallel Filter plugin execution (line 498)\n          - **schedule_one.go:573 findNodesThatPassFilters()** → Parallel filter execution\n            - Calls `fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods()` in parallel for each node (line 611)\n            - Uses `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()` to parallelize node evaluation\n        - Calls `findNodesThatPassExtenders()` - runs extender filters sequentially (line 507)\n    - Calls `prioritizeNodes()` - performs scoring (line 425)\n      - **schedule_one.go:745 prioritizeNodes()** → Scores feasible nodes\n        - Calls `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()` - extension point: PreScore (line 768)\n        - Calls `fwk.RunScorePlugins()` - extension point: Score (line 774)\n        - Calls extender Prioritize methods in parallel (line 806)\n    - Calls `selectHost()` - selects best node via reservoir sampling (line 430)\n\n- **Back in schedulingCycle():** If scheduling successful:\n  - Calls `sched.assume()` - optimistically updates cache (line 198)\n    - Updates pod.Spec.NodeName\n    - Calls `sched.Cache.AssumePod()` to mark pod as assumed in cache\n    - Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.DeleteNominatedPodIfExists()` if applicable\n  - Calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()` - extension point: Reserve (line 209)\n    - If failed: calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` and `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()`\n  - Calls `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()` - extension point: Permit (line 231)\n    - Returns Success, Wait, or rejection status\n\n### 4. Binding Cycle (Phase 2: Bind - Async Goroutine)\n**schedule_one.go:118 Launches bindingCycle() in goroutine**\n\n**schedule_one.go:265 bindingCycle()** → Asynchronously binds pod to node\n- Calls `fwk.WaitOnPermit()` - waits for Permit plugins to allow binding (line 278)\n- Calls `fwk.RunPreBindPlugins()` - extension point: PreBind (line 294)\n- Calls `sched.bind()` - performs actual binding (line 299)\n  - **schedule_one.go:958 bind()** → Executes binding\n    - Tries `sched.extendersBinding()` - extender binding if available (line 964)\n    - Calls `fwk.RunBindPlugins()` - extension point: Bind (line 968)\n- Calls `fwk.RunPostBindPlugins()` - extension point: PostBind (line 312)\n- Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.Done()` to mark pod processing complete (line 132)\n\n### 5. Failure Handling\n**schedule_one.go:113 FailureHandler()** → Called if scheduling or binding fails\n- **schedule_one.go:1013 handleSchedulingFailure()** → Handles scheduling failures\n  - Runs `fwk.RunPostFilterPlugins()` - extension point: PostFilter for preemption (line 176)\n  - Adds pod to unschedulable queue or backoff queue\n  - Updates pod condition and nominated node information\n\n**schedule_one.go:324 handleBindingCycleError()** → Handles binding failures\n- Calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` to release reservations\n- Calls `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()` to remove assumed pod\n- Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to requeue affected pods\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Two-Phase Scheduling with Optimistic Assumptions**\nThe scheduler separates scheduling into two independent phases running asynchronously:\n- **Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous)**: Finds node and reserves resources without blocking\n- **Binding Cycle (Asynchronous)**: Actually binds pod to API server in background\n\nThe key innovation is the **assume** operation: after scheduling decides a node, it optimistically assumes the pod is bound (`Cache.AssumePod()`) and updates the in-memory cache. This allows subsequent pods to be scheduled based on this assumption, without waiting for the API server to confirm binding. If binding later fails, the cache is rolled back via `Cache.ForgetPod()`.\n\n#### 2. **Plugin Framework with Extension Points**\nThe scheduler uses a sophisticated plugin architecture with **11 extension points** executed in this order:\n\n**Scheduling Cycle:**\n1. **PreEnqueue** - Filter pods before adding to queue (in queue processing)\n2. **PreFilter** - Early filtering, can reduce node set to evaluate\n3. **Filter** - Main feasibility checking (parallel)\n4. **PostFilter** - Preemption/remediation (runs if no nodes pass Filter)\n5. **PreScore** - Prepare for scoring\n6. **Score** - Rank nodes (parallel)\n7. **Reserve** - Update plugin state after selection\n\n**Binding Cycle:**\n8. **Permit** - Final approval gate, can delay binding\n9. **PreBind** - Pre-binding setup\n10. **Bind** - Actual binding to API server\n11. **PostBind** - Cleanup/notification after successful binding\n\n#### 3. **Concurrent Execution**\n- **Filter plugins run in parallel** across nodes using `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()`\n- **Score plugins run in parallel** for selected nodes\n- **Binding happens asynchronously** in a separate goroutine\n- **Multiple pods schedule concurrently** - each pod is independent, but all share the same cache\n\n#### 4. **Smart Queueing with Priority**\nThe **SchedulingQueue** manages pods with intelligent prioritization:\n- **activeQ** (heap): Primary queue of schedulable pods, ordered by QueueSort plugin\n- **backoffQ** (heap): Failed pods with exponential backoff, waiting to retry\n- **unschedulablePods**: Pods that failed scheduling, stay here until cluster state changes\n- **In-flight tracking**: Maps UID → in-flight pod entries to track which pods are currently being scheduled\n\n#### 5. **Event-Driven Requeueing with Queueing Hints**\nWhen a cluster event occurs (node added, pod updated, etc.), the scheduler uses **EnqueueExtensions** to efficiently requeue only affected pods:\n- Plugins register which events can make them pass/fail\n- On each event, only pods rejected by interested plugins are requeued\n- Reduces unnecessary retries and improves scheduling latency\n\n#### 6. **State Machine for Pod Lifecycle in Cache**\nThe cache implements a pod state machine:\n```\nInitial → Assumed → Added → Deleted\n          ↘ Expired ↗\n```\n- **Initial**: Pod not in cache\n- **Assumed**: Optimistically scheduled, in cache but not API-confirmed\n- **Added**: Pod confirmed by API server\n- **Expired**: Assumed pod timed out waiting for Add confirmation\n- **Deleted**: Pod removed from cache\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n#### **Scheduler (scheduler.go)**\n- Orchestrates the overall scheduling loop\n- Holds Cache, SchedulingQueue, Profiles\n- Manages event handlers for pod/node updates\n- Delegates scheduling to framework profiles\n\n#### **Framework (framework/runtime/framework.go)**\n- Manages plugin lifecycle (initialization, execution, cleanup)\n- Provides Run* methods for each extension point\n- Coordinates plugin execution order and error handling\n- Maintains plugin state (pluginsMap, extensions point slices)\n- Implements Handle interface for plugin callbacks\n\n#### **Cache (internal/cache/interface.go)**\n- Maintains in-memory pod and node state\n- Implements assume/forget/add/remove operations\n- Provides node info snapshots for scheduling\n- Tracks assumed pods and their expiration\n\n#### **SchedulingQueue (internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go)**\n- Manages three sub-queues of pods at different stages\n- Implements pod nomination for preemption\n- Tracks in-flight pods being processed\n- Handles backoff logic for failed pods\n- Processes cluster events to requeue pods\n\n### Data Flow During Scheduling Cycle\n\n```\n1. Pod enters queue (via pod watcher event handler)\n   ↓\n2. ScheduleOne() pops pod from queue\n   ↓\n3. Create fresh CycleState for this pod\n   ↓\n4. Scheduling Cycle:\n   4a. PreFilter plugins → optional node reduction\n   4b. Filter plugins (parallel) → feasible nodes\n   4c. PostFilter plugins (if needed) → preemption\n   4d. PreScore plugins\n   4e. Score plugins (parallel) → ranked nodes\n   4f. Reserve plugins → reserve resources\n   4g. Permit plugins → final approval\n   ↓\n5. Assume pod in cache (optimistic scheduling)\n   ↓\n6. Launch Binding Cycle asynchronously:\n   6a. WaitOnPermit → wait for gate\n   6b. PreBind plugins\n   6c. Bind plugins → API server binding\n   6d. PostBind plugins\n   6e. Mark pod Done in queue\n   ↓\n7. On failure: Unreserve, Forget, and requeue\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n#### **Plugin Interface (framework/interface.go)**\nEach plugin implements `Plugin` base interface with `Name()` method, plus one or more extension point interfaces:\n- `PreEnqueuePlugin.PreEnqueue(ctx, pod) Status`\n- `PreFilterPlugin.PreFilter(ctx, state, pod) (PreFilterResult, Status)`\n- `FilterPlugin.Filter(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo) Status`\n- `ScorePlugin.Score(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (int64, Status)`\n- `ReservePlugin.Reserve(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) Status`\n- `PermitPlugin.Permit(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (Status, time.Duration)`\n- `BindPlugin.Bind(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) Status`\n\n#### **CycleState (framework/cycle_state.go)**\nThread-safe map for storing plugin-specific state:\n- `Write(key StateKey, data StateData)` - store state\n- `Read(key StateKey) (StateData, error)` - retrieve state\n- `Clone() CycleState` - create copy for preemption scenarios\n\n#### **PodNominator (framework/interface.go)**\nManages nominated pods for preemption:\n- `AddNominatedPod(pod, nominatingInfo)` - mark pod as nominated\n- `DeleteNominatedPodIfExists(pod)` - remove nomination\n- `NominatedPodsForNode(nodeName) []PodInfo` - get nominated pods on node\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses a **two-phase pipeline (scheduling + binding) with an 11-point plugin framework** to schedule pods to nodes. Pods flow from the queue through a filtering phase (PreFilter → Filter → optional PostFilter), then a scoring phase (PreScore → Score), then reservation and permission gates. Once a node is selected, the pod is **optimistically assumed** in the cache (allowing subsequent pods to consider it), and binding happens asynchronously in a separate phase with PreBind → Bind → PostBind plugins. The architecture enables **concurrent scheduling of multiple pods** while maintaining consistency through intelligent cache management, event-driven requeueing, and transactional semantics where binding failures trigger rollback of assumptions.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":138,"cache_read_input_tokens":100800,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":138},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"736a6c56-cc6d-437a-8c99-c5b78bdd5199","uuid":"af875844-10c3-4a82-8f61-ebbdb14b4043"}

Entry Point: Main Scheduling Loop\n**scheduler.go:435 Run()** → Starts SchedulingQueue and launches main scheduling loop\n- Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.Run()` to start queue processing\n- Calls `wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)` - runs ScheduleOne repeatedly until context done\n\n### 2. Pod Retrieval & Framework Selection\n**schedule_one.go:66 ScheduleOne()** → Processes one pod per invocation\n- Calls `sched.NextPod()` (which is `podQueue.Pop()`) to get next pod from queue (line 68)\n- Calls `sched.frameworkForPod(pod)` to select the appropriate framework/profile (line 86)\n- Checks `sched.skipPodSchedule()` - skips if pod is deleted or already assumed (line 93)\n- Creates `framework.CycleState` for storing plugin state (line 101)\n\n### 3. Scheduling Cycle (Phase 1: Find & Reserve)\n**schedule_one.go:139 schedulingCycle()** → Main scheduling algorithm\n- Calls `sched.SchedulePod()` which is `sched.schedulePod()` (line 149)\n  - **schedule_one.go:390 schedulePod()** → Filters and scores nodes\n    - Calls `sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot()` to get current node state snapshot (line 393)\n    - Calls `sched.findNodesThatFitPod()` - performs filtering (line 402)\n      - **schedule_one.go:442 findNodesThatFitPod()** → Filters nodes via PreFilter, Filter, and extenders\n        - Calls `fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins()` - extension point: PreFilter (line 453)\n        - Evaluates nominated node if present (line 475)\n        - Calls `sched.findNodesThatPassFilters()` - parallel Filter plugin execution (line 498)\n          - **schedule_one.go:573 findNodesThatPassFilters()** → Parallel filter execution\n            - Calls `fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods()` in parallel for each node (line 611)\n            - Uses `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()` to parallelize node evaluation\n        - Calls `findNodesThatPassExtenders()` - runs extender filters sequentially (line 507)\n    - Calls `prioritizeNodes()` - performs scoring (line 425)\n      - **schedule_one.go:745 prioritizeNodes()** → Scores feasible nodes\n        - Calls `fwk.RunPreScorePlugins()` - extension point: PreScore (line 768)\n        - Calls `fwk.RunScorePlugins()` - extension point: Score (line 774)\n        - Calls extender Prioritize methods in parallel (line 806)\n    - Calls `selectHost()` - selects best node via reservoir sampling (line 430)\n\n- **Back in schedulingCycle():** If scheduling successful:\n  - Calls `sched.assume()` - optimistically updates cache (line 198)\n    - Updates pod.Spec.NodeName\n    - Calls `sched.Cache.AssumePod()` to mark pod as assumed in cache\n    - Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.DeleteNominatedPodIfExists()` if applicable\n  - Calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve()` - extension point: Reserve (line 209)\n    - If failed: calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` and `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()`\n  - Calls `fwk.RunPermitPlugins()` - extension point: Permit (line 231)\n    - Returns Success, Wait, or rejection status\n\n### 4. Binding Cycle (Phase 2: Bind - Async Goroutine)\n**schedule_one.go:118 Launches bindingCycle() in goroutine**\n\n**schedule_one.go:265 bindingCycle()** → Asynchronously binds pod to node\n- Calls `fwk.WaitOnPermit()` - waits for Permit plugins to allow binding (line 278)\n- Calls `fwk.RunPreBindPlugins()` - extension point: PreBind (line 294)\n- Calls `sched.bind()` - performs actual binding (line 299)\n  - **schedule_one.go:958 bind()** → Executes binding\n    - Tries `sched.extendersBinding()` - extender binding if available (line 964)\n    - Calls `fwk.RunBindPlugins()` - extension point: Bind (line 968)\n- Calls `fwk.RunPostBindPlugins()` - extension point: PostBind (line 312)\n- Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.Done()` to mark pod processing complete (line 132)\n\n### 5. Failure Handling\n**schedule_one.go:113 FailureHandler()** → Called if scheduling or binding fails\n- **schedule_one.go:1013 handleSchedulingFailure()** → Handles scheduling failures\n  - Runs `fwk.RunPostFilterPlugins()` - extension point: PostFilter for preemption (line 176)\n  - Adds pod to unschedulable queue or backoff queue\n  - Updates pod condition and nominated node information\n\n**schedule_one.go:324 handleBindingCycleError()** → Handles binding failures\n- Calls `fwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve()` to release reservations\n- Calls `sched.Cache.ForgetPod()` to remove assumed pod\n- Calls `sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to requeue affected pods\n\n## Architecture Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns\n\n#### 1. **Two-Phase Scheduling with Optimistic Assumptions**\nThe scheduler separates scheduling into two independent phases running asynchronously:\n- **Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous)**: Finds node and reserves resources without blocking\n- **Binding Cycle (Asynchronous)**: Actually binds pod to API server in background\n\nThe key innovation is the **assume** operation: after scheduling decides a node, it optimistically assumes the pod is bound (`Cache.AssumePod()`) and updates the in-memory cache. This allows subsequent pods to be scheduled based on this assumption, without waiting for the API server to confirm binding. If binding later fails, the cache is rolled back via `Cache.ForgetPod()`.\n\n#### 2. **Plugin Framework with Extension Points**\nThe scheduler uses a sophisticated plugin architecture with **11 extension points** executed in this order:\n\n**Scheduling Cycle:**\n1. **PreEnqueue** - Filter pods before adding to queue (in queue processing)\n2. **PreFilter** - Early filtering, can reduce node set to evaluate\n3. **Filter** - Main feasibility checking (parallel)\n4. **PostFilter** - Preemption/remediation (runs if no nodes pass Filter)\n5. **PreScore** - Prepare for scoring\n6. **Score** - Rank nodes (parallel)\n7. **Reserve** - Update plugin state after selection\n\n**Binding Cycle:**\n8. **Permit** - Final approval gate, can delay binding\n9. **PreBind** - Pre-binding setup\n10. **Bind** - Actual binding to API server\n11. **PostBind** - Cleanup/notification after successful binding\n\n#### 3. **Concurrent Execution**\n- **Filter plugins run in parallel** across nodes using `fwk.Parallelizer().Until()`\n- **Score plugins run in parallel** for selected nodes\n- **Binding happens asynchronously** in a separate goroutine\n- **Multiple pods schedule concurrently** - each pod is independent, but all share the same cache\n\n#### 4. **Smart Queueing with Priority**\nThe **SchedulingQueue** manages pods with intelligent prioritization:\n- **activeQ** (heap): Primary queue of schedulable pods, ordered by QueueSort plugin\n- **backoffQ** (heap): Failed pods with exponential backoff, waiting to retry\n- **unschedulablePods**: Pods that failed scheduling, stay here until cluster state changes\n- **In-flight tracking**: Maps UID → in-flight pod entries to track which pods are currently being scheduled\n\n#### 5. **Event-Driven Requeueing with Queueing Hints**\nWhen a cluster event occurs (node added, pod updated, etc.), the scheduler uses **EnqueueExtensions** to efficiently requeue only affected pods:\n- Plugins register which events can make them pass/fail\n- On each event, only pods rejected by interested plugins are requeued\n- Reduces unnecessary retries and improves scheduling latency\n\n#### 6. **State Machine for Pod Lifecycle in Cache**\nThe cache implements a pod state machine:\n```\nInitial → Assumed → Added → Deleted\n          ↘ Expired ↗\n```\n- **Initial**: Pod not in cache\n- **Assumed**: Optimistically scheduled, in cache but not API-confirmed\n- **Added**: Pod confirmed by API server\n- **Expired**: Assumed pod timed out waiting for Add confirmation\n- **Deleted**: Pod removed from cache\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n#### **Scheduler (scheduler.go)**\n- Orchestrates the overall scheduling loop\n- Holds Cache, SchedulingQueue, Profiles\n- Manages event handlers for pod/node updates\n- Delegates scheduling to framework profiles\n\n#### **Framework (framework/runtime/framework.go)**\n- Manages plugin lifecycle (initialization, execution, cleanup)\n- Provides Run* methods for each extension point\n- Coordinates plugin execution order and error handling\n- Maintains plugin state (pluginsMap, extensions point slices)\n- Implements Handle interface for plugin callbacks\n\n#### **Cache (internal/cache/interface.go)**\n- Maintains in-memory pod and node state\n- Implements assume/forget/add/remove operations\n- Provides node info snapshots for scheduling\n- Tracks assumed pods and their expiration\n\n#### **SchedulingQueue (internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go)**\n- Manages three sub-queues of pods at different stages\n- Implements pod nomination for preemption\n- Tracks in-flight pods being processed\n- Handles backoff logic for failed pods\n- Processes cluster events to requeue pods\n\n### Data Flow During Scheduling Cycle\n\n```\n1. Pod enters queue (via pod watcher event handler)\n   ↓\n2. ScheduleOne() pops pod from queue\n   ↓\n3. Create fresh CycleState for this pod\n   ↓\n4. Scheduling Cycle:\n   4a. PreFilter plugins → optional node reduction\n   4b. Filter plugins (parallel) → feasible nodes\n   4c. PostFilter plugins (if needed) → preemption\n   4d. PreScore plugins\n   4e. Score plugins (parallel) → ranked nodes\n   4f. Reserve plugins → reserve resources\n   4g. Permit plugins → final approval\n   ↓\n5. Assume pod in cache (optimistic scheduling)\n   ↓\n6. Launch Binding Cycle asynchronously:\n   6a. WaitOnPermit → wait for gate\n   6b. PreBind plugins\n   6c. Bind plugins → API server binding\n   6d. PostBind plugins\n   6e. Mark pod Done in queue\n   ↓\n7. On failure: Unreserve, Forget, and requeue\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n#### **Plugin Interface (framework/interface.go)**\nEach plugin implements `Plugin` base interface with `Name()` method, plus one or more extension point interfaces:\n- `PreEnqueuePlugin.PreEnqueue(ctx, pod) Status`\n- `PreFilterPlugin.PreFilter(ctx, state, pod) (PreFilterResult, Status)`\n- `FilterPlugin.Filter(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo) Status`\n- `ScorePlugin.Score(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (int64, Status)`\n- `ReservePlugin.Reserve(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) Status`\n- `PermitPlugin.Permit(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (Status, time.Duration)`\n- `BindPlugin.Bind(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) Status`\n\n#### **CycleState (framework/cycle_state.go)**\nThread-safe map for storing plugin-specific state:\n- `Write(key StateKey, data StateData)` - store state\n- `Read(key StateKey) (StateData, error)` - retrieve state\n- `Clone() CycleState` - create copy for preemption scenarios\n\n#### **PodNominator (framework/interface.go)**\nManages nominated pods for preemption:\n- `AddNominatedPod(pod, nominatingInfo)` - mark pod as nominated\n- `DeleteNominatedPodIfExists(pod)` - remove nomination\n- `NominatedPodsForNode(nodeName) []PodInfo` - get nominated pods on node\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses a **two-phase pipeline (scheduling + binding) with an 11-point plugin framework** to schedule pods to nodes. Pods flow from the queue through a filtering phase (PreFilter → Filter → optional PostFilter), then a scoring phase (PreScore → Score), then reservation and permission gates. Once a node is selected, the pod is **optimistically assumed** in the cache (allowing subsequent pods to consider it), and binding happens asynchronously in a separate phase with PreBind → Bind → PostBind plugins. The architecture enables **concurrent scheduling of multiple pods** while maintaining consistency through intelligent cache management, event-driven requeueing, and transactional semantics where binding failures trigger rollback of assumptions.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

This allows subsequent pods to be scheduled based on this assumption, without waiting for the API server to confirm binding. If binding later fails, the cache is rolled back via `Cache.ForgetPod()`.\n   104→\n   105→#### 2. **Plugin Framework with Extension Points**\n   106→The scheduler uses a sophisticated plugin architecture with **11 extension points** executed in this order:\n   107→\n   108→**Scheduling Cycle:**\n   109→1. **PreEnqueue** - Filter pods before adding to queue (in queue processing)\n   110→2. **PreFilter** - Early filtering, can reduce node set to evaluate\n   111→3. **Filter** - Main feasibility checking (parallel)\n   112→4. **PostFilter** - Preemption/remediation (runs if no nodes pass Filter)\n   113→5. **PreScore** - Prepare for scoring\n   114→6. **Score** - Rank nodes (parallel)\n   115→7. **Reserve** - Update plugin state after selection\n   116→\n   117→**Binding Cycle:**\n Primary queue of schedulable pods, ordered by QueueSort plugin\n   132→- **backoffQ** (heap): Failed pods with exponential backoff, waiting to retry\n   133→- **unschedulablePods**: Pods that failed scheduling, stay here until cluster state changes\n   134→- **In-flight tracking**: Maps UID → in-flight pod entries to track which pods are currently being scheduled\n   135→\n   136→#### 5. **Event-Driven Requeueing with Queueing Hints**\n   137→When a cluster event occurs (node added, pod updated, etc.), the scheduler uses **EnqueueExtensions** to efficiently requeue only affected pods:\n   138→- Plugins register which events can make them pass/fail\n   139→- On each event, only pods rejected by interested plugins are requeued\n   140→- Reduces unnecessary retries and improves scheduling latency\n   141→\n   142→#### 6. **State Machine for Pod Lifecycle in Cache**\n   143→The cache implements a pod state machine:\n   144→```\n   145→Initial → Assumed → Added → Deleted\n   146→          ↘ Expired ↗\n   147→```\n   148→- **Initial**: Pod not in cache\n   149→- **Assumed**: Optimistically scheduled, in cache but not API-confirmed\n   150→- **Added**: Pod confirmed by API server\n   151→- **Expired**: Assumed pod timed out waiting for Add confirmation\n   152→- **Deleted**: Pod removed from cache\n   153→\n   154→### Component Responsibilities\n   155→\n   156→#### **Scheduler (scheduler.go)**\n   157→- Orchestrates the overall scheduling loop\n   158→- Holds Cache, SchedulingQueue, Profiles\n   159→- Manages event handlers for pod/node updates\n   160→- processed\n   179→- Handles backoff logic for failed pods\n   180→- Processes cluster events to requeue pods\n   181→\n   182→### Data Flow During Scheduling Cycle\n   183→\n   184→```\n   185→1. Pod enters queue (via pod watcher event handler)\n   186→   ↓\n   187→2. ScheduleOne() pops pod from queue\n   188→   ↓\n   189→3. Create fresh CycleState for this pod\n   190→   ↓\n   191→4. On failure: Unreserve, Forget, and requeue\n   210→```\n   211→\n   212→### Interface Contracts\n   213→\n   214→#### **Plugin Interface (framework/interface.go)**\n   215→Each plugin implements `Plugin` base interface with `Name()` method, plus one or more extension point interfaces:\n   216→- `PreEnqueuePlugin.PreEnqueue(ctx, pod) Status`\n   217→- `PreFilterPlugin.PreFilter(ctx, state, pod) (PreFilterResult, Status)`\n   218→- `FilterPlugin.Filter(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo) Status`\n   219→- `ScorePlugin.Score(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (int64, Status)`\n   220→- `ReservePlugin.Reserve(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) Status`\n   221→- `PermitPlugin.Permit(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) (Status, time.Duration)`\n   222→- `BindPlugin.Bind(ctx, state, pod, nodeName) Status`\n   223→\n   224→#### **CycleState (framework/cycle_state.go)**\n   225→Thread-safe map for storing plugin-specific state:\n   226→- `Write(key StateKey, data StateData)` - store state\n   227→- `Read(key StateKey) (StateData, error)` - retrieve state\n   228→- `Clone() CycleState` - create copy for preemption scenarios\n   229→\n   230→#### **PodNominator (framework/interface.go)**\n   231→Manages nominated pods for preemption:\n   232→- `AddNominatedPod(pod, nominatingInfo)` - mark pod as nominated\n   233→- `DeleteNominatedPodIfExists(pod)` - remove nomination\n   234→- `NominatedPodsForNode(nodeName) []PodInfo` - get nominated pods on node\n   235→\n   236→## Summary\n   237→\n   238→The Kubernetes scheduler uses a **two-phase pipeline (scheduling + binding) with an 11-point plugin framework** to schedule pods to nodes. Pods flow from the queue through a filtering phase (PreFilter → Filter → optional PostFilter), then a scoring phase (PreScore → Score), then reservation and permission gates. Once a node is selected, the pod is **optimistically assumed** in the cache (allowing subsequent pods to consider it), and binding happens asynchronously in a separate phase with PreBind → Bind → PostBind plugins. The architecture enables **concurrent scheduling of multiple pods** while maintaining consistency through intelligent cache management, event-driven requeueing, and transactional semantics where binding failures trigger rollback of assumptions.\n   239→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
